<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_947c3b4d-78d3-4d62-bfe9-785908cd32ac'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer4231479420998156087">Feyre's survival rests upon her ability to hunt and kill – the forest where she lives is a cold, bleak place in the long winter months.   <span id="freeText4231479420998156087" style="display:none">Feyre's survival rests upon her ability to hunt and kill – the forest where she lives is a cold, bleak place in the long winter months. So when she spots a deer in the forest being pursued by a wolf, she cannot resist fighting it for the flesh. But to do so, she must kill the predator and killing something so precious comes at a price ...<br /><br />Dragged to a magical kingdom for the murder of a faerie, Feyre discovers that her captor, his face obscured by a jewelled mask, is hiding far more than his piercing green eyes would suggest. Feyre's presence at the court is closely guarded, and as she begins to learn why, her feelings for him turn from hostility to passion and the faerie lands become an even more dangerous place. Feyre must fight to break an ancient curse, or she will lose him forever.</span>

Toward the end? I have this theory that maybe Rhysand recognizes that she might possibly be his mate, and that threw him as a surprise, that's why he was so shocked? I might be trying to look into something that might not be there, but is anyone else curious?<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_767048578" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/767048578" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/767048578?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer767048578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2329826492794141608"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434467354ra/15225852.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Clearly I'm in the minority here. DNF at 30% because I just got fed up with things moving at a snail's pace and NOT MAKING SENSE AT ALL. This was one of the most uncompelling versions of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> that I have ever read. The writing is nothing outstanding, there was nothing that moved me. I felt <i>Cruel Beauty</i> among other B&B retellings I've read this year and last have done a far superior job at moving me emotionally.<br/><br/>Look, I'm sure by the end of the book, all the things tie together and</span>
  <span id="freeText2329826492794141608" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434467354ra/15225852.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Clearly I'm in the minority here. DNF at 30% because I just got fed up with things moving at a snail's pace and NOT MAKING SENSE AT ALL. This was one of the most uncompelling versions of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> that I have ever read. The writing is nothing outstanding, there was nothing that moved me. I felt <i>Cruel Beauty</i> among other B&amp;B retellings I've read this year and last have done a far superior job at moving me emotionally.<br><br>Look, I'm sure by the end of the book, all the things tie together and everything's just dandy and things will make sense, and I'd be like "ooooooh, so that's why ____." Me, I don't care. Ain't nobody got time for that. I have so many questions and I'm just fed up. This is not a retelling of Beauty and the Beast. This is a book about a girl who gets to live an easy life with a guy who's implied to be a gorgeous Fae underneath his mask.<br><br>The original story makes sense: here's roughly how it goes. Handsome prince is cursed to be ugly unless he gets a chick to fall for him. Flash forward, there's Belle's dad. Belle's dad wanders into Beast's castle and touches his stuff. Beast doesn't like the fact that Belle's dad touched his stuff. Beast is going to kill Belle's dad unless he gets Beast some pussy. Belle's valiantly steps in to save dad, Beast is as nice to her as much as a hairy ugly, self-conscious, socially ostracized monster can be. Belle is treated like a princess because Beast really, really fucking needs her to save him and his people before the curse runs out!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434466894ra/15225752.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There's a reason Belle is treated like the queen! Things make sense! They have to learn to trust one another. Things are slowly developed an built over time. There is a hideous beast who is scarred emotionally, and a beauty who needs to look past the exterior. There is a point. Not so with this book. <b>Things are far, far too easy with this book.</b><br><br>Now here's this version of Beauty and the Beast, <b>a retelling that tries to be bad-ass and fails completely,</b> from the little that I have read.<br><br>There's <b>Feyre</b> who has a pretty crappy life with an absentminded, worthless, spineless dad, and two of the most bitchy, ungrateful sisters in the entire world. She slaves for them, she hunts food for them, she works her ass off for them. Without her, their family would starve. They don't care. I feel some pity for her, but she acts like so much of a martyr that there's only so much I can take.<br><br>While hunting one day, Feyre kills a wolf, well, surprise, surprise, that wolf turns out to be a Fae in disguise. In return for this kill, Feyre is taken by a wolf (who's a Fae in disguise) away from her family.<blockquote>
  <i>“What is the payment the Treaty requires?”<br><br>His eyes didn’t leave my face as he said, “A life for a life. Any unprovoked attacks on faerie-kind by humans are to be paid only by a human life in exchange.”</i>
</blockquote><b>A life for a life!</b> Oh, no! Is she going to die?! That's what a life for a life means, right? <b>WRONG</b>. Feyre is taken off to magical Fairyland to live in luxury for the rest of her life while her family is taken care of back in their little village.<blockquote>
  <i>“Some would say it’s unwise to insult a Fae in his home,” Tamlin ground out. “Some would say you should be grateful for me finding you before another one of my kind came to claim the debt, for sparing your life and then offering you the chance to live in comfort.”</i>
</blockquote>So what?! <b>Why?!</b> This makes no sense at all. <b>Feyre kills one of their kind. A beloved brother.</b> In exchange, there is <b>absolutely no punishment whatsoever</b>. She gets to live in a fantastically fabulous castle, waited on by servants. She gets beautiful clothes and delicious food.<blockquote>
  <i>Another useless answer. I dug into my breakfast, savoring each rich sip of tea, and she slipped into the bathing chamber. When I was done eating and bathing, I refused Alis’s offer and dressed myself in another exquisite tunic—this one of purple so deep it could have been black.</i>
</blockquote>Clearly there is some kind of a setup involving The Treaty, since there seems to be a lot of secrecy between the Fae...<b>but wait, whatever information she wants, the Fae reveals...they're revealing their own weakness to Feyre, who is constantly plotting her own escape.</b> It doesn't make any sense!<blockquote>
  <i> “There is … a sickness in these lands. Across Prythian. There has been for almost fifty years now. It is why this house and these lands are so empty: most have left. The blight spreads slowly, but it has made magic act … strangely. My own powers are diminished due to it. These masks”—he tapped on his—“are the result of a surge of it that occurred during a masquerade forty-nine years ago. Even now, we can’t remove them.”</i>
</blockquote>Over and over and over, <b>the Fae reveal their secrets to her, including one that might help her escape</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>“So there are faeries who will actually answer any question if you trap them?” Maybe they’d know how to free me from the Treaty’s terms.<br>“Yes,” he said tightly. “The Suriel. But they’re old and wicked, and not worth the danger of going out to find them.</i>
</blockquote>And then pretty much the next chapter, she goes out AND IMMEDIATELY FINDS THESE MYSTERIOUS CREATURES. WHAT THE FUCK.<br><br>I do not like it when things come so easily to a main character, and everything comes easily to Feyre. There is no consequence whatsoever to her actions. There is no punishment to her deed of killing. The Fae are supposed to hate her...it doesn't feel like it, because she is "inconsequential." In fact, they're more of her playmates than her wardens. The Fae seem to have no other things to do besides play with her and hunt with her.<blockquote>
  <i>“My morning work was postponed,” he said. Indeed, his usual tunic was off, the baldric gone, and the sleeves of his white shirt had been rolled up to the elbows to reveal tanned forearms corded with muscle. “If you want a ride across the grounds—if you’re interested in your new … residence, I can take you.”</i>
</blockquote>And teach her how to read and write...because Feyre cannot read or write, an ironic twist to the Disney Belle's love for reading.<blockquote>
  <i>“I could help you write to them, if that’s why you’re in here.”</i>
</blockquote>Feyre is irreverent, ungrateful and insulting to her wardens...in a way that gets her no punishment whatsoever.<blockquote>
  <i>“Do you ever stop being such a prick?” I snapped back.<br><br>Dead—really, truly, I should have been dead for that.<br><br>But Lucien grinned at me. “Much better.”</i>
</blockquote>As I said, I'm sure this book improves in the end, but from what I've read, this book makes no sense, the writing is emotionless, the characters are flat, the main character unrealistic, and I do not care to continue.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2329826492794141608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_709919362" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/709919362" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/709919362?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer709919362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3172142180010510913"><b>2 1/2 stars.</b> Maybe my rating comes as a surprise or even - if you care - a disappointment, but let me assure you: no one is more surprised or disappointed than I am. <br/><br/>I've had this book on my TBR ever since it appeared on Goodreads without a title, cover or description. I started reading it as soon as it became available and the array of positive reviews from my friends and strangers alike made me feel sure I would love it. But I didn't. It is possible I expected all the wrong things from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_' title='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court</a></span>
  <span id="freeText3172142180010510913" style="display:none"><b>2 1/2 stars.</b> Maybe my rating comes as a surprise or even - if you care - a disappointment, but let me assure you: no one is more surprised or disappointed than I am. <br /><br />I've had this book on my TBR ever since it appeared on Goodreads without a title, cover or description. I started reading it as soon as it became available and the array of positive reviews from my friends and strangers alike made me feel sure I would love it. But I didn't. It is possible I expected all the wrong things from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>, and maybe my review can prevent others from doing the same.<br /><br /><b>Here's what I expected:</b> an intricate fantasy world, supernatural politics and alliances, fast-paced action, a sensual romance - perhaps similar to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a> and other <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> retellings, and a flawed but likable heroine.<br /><br />But this book is, if you ask me, nothing more or less than <b>softcore erotica</b>. Which is fine, if that's what you're looking for. <br /><br />I personally thought that the fantasy aspect felt like trimmings around a story that was all about a romance between Feyre (the narrator) and Tamlin (a High Lord of the Fae). There are some titillating scenes where Tamlin bites Feyre's neck and they have sex - undoubtedly the best bits of the book and I won't pretend I didn't feel a little hot under the collar myself. But the "ancient wicked shadow" promised in the blurb is only really a source of more romantic angst for Feyre and Tamlin.<br /><br />However, I *do* like a good romance as much as anyone, so there are other reasons this book didn't quite work for me. In order to express what I mean, I'm going to compare <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a>, which is, in my opinion, a better book. <br /><br />In CB, I felt the chemistry between Nyx and Ignifex as soon as their loaded banter started to fill the pages. They were sexy together, Ignifex was an evil ruler (which was a real problem for their relationship) with blood-red eyes, and the supernatural part of the book was creepy, weird and completely unique. Despite enjoying the actual non-PG scenes in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a>, I never felt any real chemistry between Feyre and Tamlin or any realistic challenge to their relationship.<br /><br /><b>What makes <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> such a compelling romance?</b> One that demands to be told over and over again in so many different ways? I'll tell you what it is: it's the obstacles, the challenges, the improbability... <i>how can a young woman come to love an ugly beast?</i> We ask. <i>I'll prove it's possible!</i> The author replies. That's why readers fall in love with the beast again and again, even when he is furry and has horns like the Disney version. I loved the Disney beast. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And that badass fox in Robin Hood so it's possible I have issues. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Tamlin is not a beast.</b><br /><br /><i>“Even as he bit out the words, I couldn’t ignore the sheer male beauty of that strong jaw, the richness of his golden-tan skin.”</i> <br /><br />Oh my, how could a poor young woman ever love a pretty-faced, golden-haired, completely not evil Fae prince? How weird.<br /><br />Maas is a good writer and the beginning - before Feyre is taken to the Fae world - made me believe a great book was on the way. When Maas writes action, she writes action <b>really</b> well. But there was far too little of it in this book. It came in behind the descriptions of beautiful Fae men and the Fae palace. <br /><br />In short: <b>It just wasn't nasty enough.</b> In truth, this felt more like an extended Cinderella retelling than what it was supposed to be. A girl lives in poverty and looks after her rather annoying sisters until one day she is swept up by a prince who takes her to his beautiful palace (after about three chapters). I just find it hard to recommend this when I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty" title="Cruel Beauty by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a> is similar and yet so much better.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3172142180010510913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2277418351" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2277418351" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2277418351?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall">2018-finer-books-club-reading-chall</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=best-of-decade">best-of-decade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2277418351" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18054147389836742205"><blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589734946i/29494799._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>If you've ever wondered which literary world would be the best to live in, wonder no longer, cause there's a <b><u><a href='https://youtu.be/SREpUj0py9o' rel='nofollow noopener'>BookTube Video</a></u></b> to answer that!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b>:----------<br/><br/>Update - 12/6/19<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Should</i>
</b> I cross the insurmountable TBR? Or reread this series again?<br/><br/><b>I think you know the answer</b><br/><br/>----------<br/><br/>Here's the original review:<blockquote>
<img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534181586i/26122701._SY540_.jpg' width='375' height='375' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </blockquote><b> Feyre is hunting </b>in the middle of the woods to<b> keep her useless starving family alive</b> (Hunger Games, anyone?). <br/><br/> A chance encounter with a wolf - who wasn't entirely a wolf </span>
  <span id="freeText18054147389836742205" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1589734946i/29494799._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>If you've ever wondered which literary world would be the best to live in, wonder no longer, cause there's a <b><u><a href="https://youtu.be/SREpUj0py9o" rel="nofollow noopener">BookTube Video</a></u></b> to answer that!</blockquote><b>
  <u>The Written Review</u>
</b>:----------<br><br>Update - 12/6/19<br><br><b>
  <i>Should</i>
</b> I cross the insurmountable TBR? Or reread this series again?<br><br><b>I think you know the answer</b><br><br>----------<br><br>Here's the original review:<blockquote>
<img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534181586i/26122701._SY540_.jpg" width="375" height="375" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </blockquote><b> Feyre is hunting </b>in the middle of the woods to<b> keep her useless starving family alive</b> (Hunger Games, anyone?). <br><br> A chance encounter with a wolf - who wasn't entirely a wolf - leaves Feyre <b>on the wrong end of an ancient treaty. </b><br><br>She is forced to go to the fairy realm to live out the remaining years of her human life - <b>no friends, no family and no freedom.</b> <blockquote>
  <i>“Has anyone ever taken care of you?” he asked quietly.<br>“No.” I’d long since stopped feeling sorry for myself about it.</i>
</blockquote>At first, she cannot think of anything but escape. Slowly (but surely), she is swept into the fairy realm - <b>in its magic &amp; intrigue, in its danger &amp; hopelessness, and in its wonder &amp; glory. </b><blockquote>
  <i>“Spring, Summer, Autumn, Winter, Dawn, Day, and Night,” it mused, as if I hadn’t even answered. “The seven Courts of Prythian, each ruled by a High Lord, all of them deadly in their own way. They are not merely powerful—they are Power.”</i>
</blockquote>Feyre lands in the Spring court - which is under a<b> masquerade curse</b> for nearly fifty years.<br><br> The court is being attacked by all manner of terrible creatures and there is a <b>blight upon the land </b>.<br><br> This blight will soon cross to the human realm - threatening everyone Feyre holds dear.<br><br><b>The first half sucks<i> but keep reading</i></b><br><br>There's no way around it. From page 1 to about 200, Feyre is <b> annoying and obstinate.</b> <br><br>I nearly put this book down half a dozen times (it was like reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22328546.Red_Queen__Red_Queen___1_" title="Red Queen (Red Queen, #1) by Victoria Aveyard" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Queen</a>).<br><br> BUT, there was something about it that kept me interested. <br><b><br>AND THANK GOODNESS FOR THAT. </b><br><br>Because wow. Seriously wow. <br><br>Midway through the book, <b>things turned around magnificently.</b> It was like a whole new book. <br><br>Sarah J Maas is a devious little thing. <br><br>Suddenly, all the plot holes, nonsensical actions of her fairy captors (Tamlin and Lucien) and Feyre's complete idiocy flipped on their heads.<b><br><br> Everything makes sense now. </b> I literally could not put this down.<br><br>Though, and maybe it's just me, but <b>the Tamlin-Feyre arc felt a bit rushed/forced.</b> Her constant love declarations really had me questioning their relationship. But then again, I had a friend who accidentally spilled the beans on that one.<br><br> Without giving any spoilers, I sure hope book 2 does a <b>complete character shift</b> on you-know-who (NOT voldemort) because I am <b>not pleased</b> with the way the love interest was hinted at during the end of the book. (He's such a jerk!)<br><br>Overall, I am <i>amazed </i>by how much effort Sarah J. Maas put into constructing this story. I'm this close || to rereading the book solely to better appreciate all those little clues that I must have passed over. <br><br>So, if you pick this up and just aren't feeling it - <b>
  <u>
    <i>keep reading</i>
  </u>
</b> - trust me. <br><br><i>The Finer Books Club - 2018 Reading Challenge: A book recommended by a friend</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads</span>

<div id="review_1088896139" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088896139" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1088896139?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairies">fairies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-hate-relationships">love-hate-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=can-t-wait-to-read-it">can-t-wait-to-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=beauty-and-the-beast">beauty-and-the-beast</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1088896139" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7933095327282103024"><strong>A richly imagined fairy tale retelling of <em>Beauty and the Beast</em>!</strong><br/><br/>If you’re a lover of retellings mingling romance, danger, faerie mystical creatures and a heroine that shows a significant deal of courage throughout, then this is one title you will not want to miss out and will very likely considerably enjoy.<br/><br/>The world-building is inventive and detailed. The different Courts of faeries are an element that adds great originality to this story. At first, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_' title='A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> might appear simila</span>
  <span id="freeText7933095327282103024" style="display:none"><strong>A richly imagined fairy tale retelling of <em>Beauty and the Beast</em>!</strong><br><br>If you’re a lover of retellings mingling romance, danger, faerie mystical creatures and a heroine that shows a significant deal of courage throughout, then this is one title you will not want to miss out and will very likely considerably enjoy.<br><br>The world-building is inventive and detailed. The different Courts of faeries are an element that adds great originality to this story. At first, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Thorns and Roses</a> might appear similar to plenty of fantasy books already written out there but, the further you read, the more you come to descry its ingenious lines shaping the well-known classic sprinkled with beautiful themes and… <strong>sensuality</strong>.<br><br>What was missing for me was action. I wanted more of it, as well as some adventure and deadly dangerous situations, which we do get, in the first chapters, but otherwise not until a good part of the novel. The pacing is quite slow, for the author chose to take her time building the relationship between Feyre, Tamlin, Lucien and even Alis, a servant. Surprisingly, there weren’t as many characters as I expected. The world-building being focused on distinct Courts principally ruled by High Lords and dwelt by lesser faeries, I thought, deceptively so, that we were going to be introduced to so many of them!<br><br>I have to say that Sarah J. Maas’ writing is compelling. While she could have moderated her descriptions of paintings, for there were many of them and relatively long ones, even those didn’t bore me. Feyre, the heroine, is both a huntress and painter. Never have I seen this mix of skills before in one person. Her strength won’t go unnoticed and neither will her dauntlessness. There were moments in the story when I felt the need to growl at her, for her difficulty to obey orders – even if for her own protection – was bewildering!<br><br>It’s true what they say, Tamlin <em>will</em> make you swoon… *wink*<br><br><strong>Recommended to fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15839984.Cruel_Beauty__Cruel_Beauty_Universe___1_" title="Cruel Beauty (Cruel Beauty Universe, #1) by Rosamund Hodge" rel="nofollow noopener">Cruel Beauty</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/161887.East" title="East by Edith Pattou" rel="nofollow noopener">East</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41424.Beauty_A_Retelling_of_the_Story_of_Beauty_and_the_Beast" title="Beauty A Retelling of the Story of Beauty and the Beast by Robin McKinley" rel="nofollow noopener">Beauty</a>.</strong><br><br>--------------------------<br>2016/06/29: Rating upped to 5 stars after second read.<br>--------------------------<br><br>Well, well, what do we have here?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1414163276l/16096824.jpg" width="500" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><strong>Original, amazingly looking cover?</strong> <em>Check!</em><br><br>‘‘Tamlin—one of the lethal, immortal faeries who once ruled their world.’’<br><br><strong>Fairies?</strong> <em>Check!</em><br><br>‘‘treacherous magical land she only knows about from legends’’<br><br><strong>Magic + alternative world + some mystery perhaps?</strong> <em>Check!</em><br><br>‘‘her feelings for Tamlin transform from icy hostility into a fiery passion’’<br><br><strong>Love/hate relationship that, because it’s Sarah J. Maas, will blow our mind?</strong> <em>Check!</em><br><br>‘‘But an ancient, wicked shadow over the faerie lands is growing, and Feyre must find a way to stop it ... or doom Tamlin—and his world—forever.’’<br><br><strong>DANGER. Brave heroine?</strong> <em>CHECK CHECK CHECK!</em><br><br><u>Basically, it has everything to look for in a fantasy.</u><br><br>Please, do not disappoint.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414253210ra/11630061.gif" width="500" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="7933095327282103024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=may">may</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2745288-wendy-darling?shelf=retellings-and-inspirations">retellings-and-inspirations</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer848952002" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1582361640938255912"><b>4.5 stars</b> Tamlin is going to set your loins aflame. Phew! My cheeks are still flushed. <br/><br/>I'm also fairly confident this book is going to help change the face of new adult fiction. How awesome to see gifted writers shaping non-contemporary stories that have the coming of age/youthful perspective and vibe of YA books and combine that with the freedom that writing for an older target audience affords them. If you liked the mood and romance of (the excellent) CRUEL BEAUTY but perhaps mourned the misse</span>
  <span id="freeText1582361640938255912" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b> Tamlin is going to set your loins aflame. Phew! My cheeks are still flushed. <br /><br />I'm also fairly confident this book is going to help change the face of new adult fiction. How awesome to see gifted writers shaping non-contemporary stories that have the coming of age/youthful perspective and vibe of YA books and combine that with the freedom that writing for an older target audience affords them. If you liked the mood and romance of (the excellent) CRUEL BEAUTY but perhaps mourned the missed opportunities of such a seductive premise, ACOTAR more than satisfies. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ BITE MY NECK SOME MORE, SIR.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Plus stunning action and gorgeous imagery and interesting characters, including a fascinating anti-hero I'm looking forward to learning more about. Serious Darkling vibes, my friends. <br /><br />Maybe more of a review closer to release. If I can calm my racing pulse before then. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1582361640938255912" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2828580075?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Teodora " class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Teodora " href="/user/show/69603149-teodora"> Teodora </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2828580075" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4085912365070113823">4.45/5 ⭐<br/><br/><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href='https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/07/14/a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-1-by-sarah-j-maas/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br/><br/><i>
  <b>This book’s mood song match – <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gXq-14lV79s' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fix You by Coldplay</a></b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587376172i/29324167._SY540_.jpg' width='275' height='373' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>mum</b>: *enters kitchen at 3 am* What the hell are you doing?<br/><b>me</b>: *with a bowl of ice cream in one hand and ACOTAR in the other* I'm starting another SJM series<br/><b>mum</b>: Hang on, I have a bottle of vodka here somewhere<br/><br/>*<br/><br/>And if this is not some relatable shit when facing Sarah J. Maas’s books then I don’t know what to tell you anymore. You puzzle me.<br/><br/>So, there you go – another great universe erected by </span>
  <span id="freeText4085912365070113823" style="display:none">4.45/5 ⭐<br><br><b>Full review on my Blog:</b> <a href="https://thedacianshewolf.home.blog/2020/07/14/a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-1-by-sarah-j-maas/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dacian She-Wolf</a> 🐺<br><br><i>
  <b>This book’s mood song match – <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gXq-14lV79s" rel="nofollow noopener">Fix You by Coldplay</a></b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587376172i/29324167._SY540_.jpg" width="275" height="373" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>mum</b>: *enters kitchen at 3 am* What the hell are you doing?<br><b>me</b>: *with a bowl of ice cream in one hand and ACOTAR in the other* I'm starting another SJM series<br><b>mum</b>: Hang on, I have a bottle of vodka here somewhere<br><br>*<br><br>And if this is not some relatable shit when facing Sarah J. Maas’s books then I don’t know what to tell you anymore. You puzzle me.<br><br>So, there you go – another great universe erected by SJM just in front of our humble eyes. She is building her own fucking multiverse and we are here to witness the power of a goddess at work. I will make three sacrifices for that.<br><br>This is, so far, for me, the best Beauty and the Beast reimagination.<br><br><b>HER EXECUTION STYLE IS THE AIR TO MY LUNGS.</b><br>And this one is not even the best of her works.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>“Magic – everything was magic, and it broke my heart.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>Mainly, our action is happening at the Spring Court where our main character finds herself in front of a new intriguing life. Or at least as intriguing as a Court of flowery gardens can be.<br><br>As I always say about SJM’s books, <b>the characters are the ones who make the action</b>. It’s like they are the very engine of a plot.<br><br>I kind of like <b>Feyre</b>. She definitely has her own personal issues, mainly because she is broken and lonely and desperate to beat her status. She is human and miserable, mainly because her family is horrible. Her whole family was created to look like the typical fairytale family – an absent coward of a father, an uninterested mother, a sister full of wicked hatred and another one caught up in her own world, sensitive and naïve. Until her sisters do something worthy of my affection, I ain’t changing my mind about them.<br><br><b>Lucien</b> (the Emissary of the Spring Court), I must say, I liked from the very beginning, but he somehow managed to grow on me. There was something likeable about him at first and he only proved that to me more as the action went on.<br><br><b>Tamlin</b>, the High Lord of the Spring Court, on the other hand, seemed a bit stiff the whole book, even though I sometimes appreciated the occasional softness of his heart.<br><br>But full-on honesty now – the <i>best</i> thing about this book, the one thing that made it 110% better was <b>Rhysand</b>. He won for this book a full star from me with all of his domineering prick moves. He played the bad boy role so good that my traitorous heart enjoyed him whole. I might have a problem but oh, what a perfect problem he is.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587376172i/29324168.png" width="205" height="355" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>
  <b>“His voice was a lover’s purr that sent shivers through me, caressing every muscle and bone and nerve.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>Sexy.<br><br>Rhysand and Feyre certainly have a sort of total chemistry that it seems Feyre doesn’t have with Tamlin; not even after they <i>supposedly</i> fell in love with each other. I don’t buy that love for more than a second and by the end when everything seemed to try to make me believe their relationship I was still not convinced.<br><br>I recognise fabulous chemistry when I see one and that ain’t it. Rhysand, you’d better act up, love, I have expectations. You’re more than just a cruel, beautiful ruffian, I know it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492518907ra/22524592.gif" width="370" height="216" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There’s a certain cruelty in this book, so very Maas. I sometimes feel like I’m reading the words of a psychopath, but then I remind myself how much I <i>enjoy</i> this cruelty in these books and I temperate myself.<br><br>That crazy wretch Amarantha is definitely the embodiment of cold murder and torture in this book and this is visible when it comes to how much her actions affect the other characters’ moods and movements. It’s terribly interesting though to see how terrified all of them can become when facing her.<br><br>But by the end, there was this sliver of hope that lingered. And that broke the evil to pieces.<br><br><br><i>
  <b>“This wasn’t music to dance to – it was music to worship, music to feel in the gaps of my soul, to bring me to a place where there was no pain.”</b>
</i><br><br><br>Even though I think this is not the best of SJM’s works, I still believe is so very good that just makes you want to know more. It leaves you craving. And in my humble opinion, that’s a bonus factor in books.<br><br>All and all, my first step into the ACOTAR universe has been a success. More steps to come. Until I fall in love. Wholly and irrevocably.<br><br>(<a href="https://urcdn.eu/styles/06daab28-7e55-4e4d-aea9-97466a8069ae_original?b" rel="nofollow noopener">Book-styled</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4085912365070113823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2350193321" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2350193321" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2350193321?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/77602709-maria?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2350193321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17804141713331183887"><b>4.8</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><blockquote>“Don't feel bad for one moment about doing what brings you joy.” </blockquote><br/><br/>I'm speechless. What am I supposed to say after this? Am I supposed to write a coherent review with vital points as to why this book WAS FUCKING AMAZING??? I CAN'T EVEN TALK RIGHT NOW I'M SPEECHLESS. I WANT THE SECOND BOOK IN MY HANDS BUT MY ORDER STILL HASN'T COME. I'M READY TO GO TO FUCKING ENGLAND MYSELF AND PURCHASE IT. KIDS I'M LITERALLY DYING HERE. <br/><br/><i>The Beauty and the Beast-esque fantasy drama tells t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17804141713331183887" style="display:none"><b>4.8</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><blockquote>“Don't feel bad for one moment about doing what brings you joy.” </blockquote><br /><br />I'm speechless. What am I supposed to say after this? Am I supposed to write a coherent review with vital points as to why this book WAS FUCKING AMAZING??? I CAN'T EVEN TALK RIGHT NOW I'M SPEECHLESS. I WANT THE SECOND BOOK IN MY HANDS BUT MY ORDER STILL HASN'T COME. I'M READY TO GO TO FUCKING ENGLAND MYSELF AND PURCHASE IT. KIDS I'M LITERALLY DYING HERE. <br /><br /><i>The Beauty and the Beast-esque fantasy drama tells the story of Feyre, who finds herself entwined with faeries after unknowingly killing one. When the 19-year-old huntress kills a wolf in the woods, a beast-like creature arrives to demand retribution for it. Dragged to a treacherous magical land she only knows about from legends, Feyre discovers that her captor is not an animal, but Tamlin, one of the lethal, immortal faeries who once ruled their world. Feyre must find a way to stop it or doom Tamlin and his world forever.</i><br /><br />I'm not a fantasy fan. I love fantasy in film and tv but not in books. I picked up this book cause I wanted to use it for my thesis for uni (don't even ask) and now after I graduated I decided to give it a go. My favorite genres to read are historical fiction and contemporary, and fantasy falls on a very different category. But the fantasy in this book man... it gripped me tight and didn't let me go.<br /><br />First I started off this book a bit confused. The language confused me a bit, the terms, all the information. I'm reading books in English while my native language is Greek so fantasy fell a bit harsh on me. As I said, I'm not a fantasy fan, and with fantasy comes many weird words and shit like that. But I kept going and after a while I got used to everything and started to enjoy the plot and the characters. I enjoyed very much the factor that there weren't many characters in this book. I don't like when a book is crowded with characters, it doesn't give me the space to love them all. This book succeeded in making all the characters lovable for me... even Rhysand. I fucking love Rhysand man. Unexpected feelings happening.<br /><br />The world <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3433047.Sarah_J__Maas" title="Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah J. Maas</a> created is so rich and dark and gloomy but also happy and hopeful and full of light, I truly enjoyed reading about it. I always get bored, to be honest, with descriptions and politics of different worlds but this one excited me. Even the fucking politics were exciting. I want to delve more into this world wHEN MY FUCKING BOOK ARRIVES.<br /><br />Now to the juicy shit... the romance. Holy fucking shit. I ship these two so hard I can't even breathe. When he sent her away I wanted to scream! He gave her a good fucking and left her hanging. Why am I laughing at this? But honestly, the romance was amazing. At first, I felt like the entire book was only gonna be about the romance and I didn't quite enjoy that but after all the revelations and the twists in the plot, the romance was used wisely. And I didn't expect that, because I have heard lots of things about this book. And now we have Rhysand... this dark, handsome motherfucker who has a gloomy past. This will become a triangle, I can feel it in my bones. But I'm here for it, for some reason. I love the heat Maas's romances convey in me.<br /><br />To sum it all up, this book took me a while to get into but it was all worth it. Maybe after this book I will start reading more fantasy. Maybe. Maybe not. As I'm waiting for the sequel to arrive, I will drawn my sorrow into crying about how amazing this first book was. Or maybe reread some parts. Maybe. Anyway, till the next one K BYE!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17804141713331183887" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1732941407?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1732941407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7100762240612960192">This was so much better the second time around. I found I wasn't so concerned about rushing through to get to the next book; since I already knew what happens I was able to savor the details and carve out a tiny piece of my heart for Tam Tam (but not really because duh). On to the next one!<br/><br/>3.5 STARS <br/><br/>I am 100% embarrassed by how much I loved this book. Everything in the Humphrey household is going awry so it was wonderful being able to escape in Feyre's exciting problems and leave my own behind. </span>
  <span id="freeText7100762240612960192" style="display:none">This was so much better the second time around. I found I wasn't so concerned about rushing through to get to the next book; since I already knew what happens I was able to savor the details and carve out a tiny piece of my heart for Tam Tam (but not really because duh). On to the next one!<br /><br />3.5 STARS <br /><br />I am 100% embarrassed by how much I loved this book. Everything in the Humphrey household is going awry so it was wonderful being able to escape in Feyre's exciting problems and leave my own behind. There is nothing of substance to the book; it is fluffy, cheesy, and has been done multiple times over before, yet somehow I STILL was completely sucked in and couldn't put it down. I ate it up like candy and am looking forward to picking up ACOMAF. <br /><br />Holy cow I fell for Rhys so hard and WHY DO I ALWAYS LIKE THE ONE THAT THE GIRL NEVER PICKS?!?!?!?! I found myself utterly bored and despising the scenes with Feyre's father and sisters. I know they were necessary, but I almost put the book down as a DNF early on bc I could hardly get through those scenes. Not sure what else I can add that hasn't been said already a million times over, but this is a reheated "Beauty and the Beast" with side dishes of Cinderella and Twilight. (I'm still thinking about Thanksgiving food-sorry guys). I might hold off on the next book until a little closer to May so I'm not left hanging. My inner teenage fangirl is looking forward to gobbling up more delicious fluff.</span>

<div id="review_1051714561" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1051714561" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1051714561?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1051714561" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3696649043092043334">I cannot remember ever being this conflicted over a book. There are parts of A Court of Thorns and Roses I really loved, but a lot of parts I really hated. <br/><br/>I went into this book fully expecting to love it. Beauty and the Beast is one of my favorite fairy tales, and I was interested to see how SJM made the story her own. <br/><br/>First off, my biggest problem with this story was Feyre as a character. I have never been so irritated. Her character development and personality, for the most part, didn't make </span>
  <span id="freeText3696649043092043334" style="display:none">I cannot remember ever being this conflicted over a book. There are parts of A Court of Thorns and Roses I really loved, but a lot of parts I really hated. <br /><br />I went into this book fully expecting to love it. Beauty and the Beast is one of my favorite fairy tales, and I was interested to see how SJM made the story her own. <br /><br />First off, my biggest problem with this story was Feyre as a character. I have never been so irritated. Her character development and personality, for the most part, didn't make sense to me. She was the caretaker of her entire family for years, supposedly a hunter with a strong survival instinct. And yet, she proceeded to make the stupidest decisions and put herself in danger time and time again. I didn't get the sense that she did this out of bravery, but more out of stupidity. It didn't mesh with what her character was supposed to be. Examples of these idiotic choices: <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ 1. Repeatedly plotting to escape into a faerie land that she knew to be deadly, when she was asleep on the way to the manor and obviously wouldn't know her way back to the mortal lands <br />2. Running after the illusion of her CRIPPLED father at NIGHT, when she has been told and witnessed how deceptive fae can be<br />3. Trapping a Suriel with little more than a snare, in the deadly part of the forest, after she has been told, and AGAIN, SEEN how dangerous these creatures are<br />4. Going to Fire Night after being told how dangerous it is, not leaving after being almost raped by 3 faeries, and then proceeding to leave her room AGAIN afterwards<br />5. Drinking the faerie wine at the Solstice, even after Lucien of all people warned her not to <br />6. Leaving the manor when the Suriel flat out TOLD her not to and that she would be safe with Tamlin, and deciding to not mention that to ANYONE before he forced her to leave <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />In addition to all of these idiotic choices, she also is incredibly inconsistent. She'll go from hating Fae to sympathizing with them to loving them back to fearing them at the drop of a hat. These inconsistencies are probably the most irritating, as there are scenes that I absolutely adore with Feyre, but then she goes back to doing the next pain in the ass thing on the next page. <br /><br />I also found her relationship with Tamlin to be problematic. Yes, I do enjoy problematic things (especially ships from time to time) but there were a lot of things I couldn't excuse with them. Again, more inconsistencies in characters' behavior. Tamlin's hot and cold behavior was eventually explained, but not until 70% of the way through the book. It was too little too late. Also, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I found the Fire Night scene to be a problem for me. I do enjoy volatile relationships and bad boy characters. But only when we are told from the beginning that one of the characters is "bad". Tamlin we are led to believe is a saint, then he bites her and gets possessive, but all is forgiven the next morning. Because he's a "nice guy." No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />The world building I found to be lackluster in a lot of ways. While I really enjoyed the wide variety of Fae creatures we got to see, I thought that a lot of the back story was revealed in a lazy way. Instead of having Feyre figure anything out for herself, important things are told to her through long monologues from a number of characters throughout the book. This happens numerous times. <br /><br />Additionally, few side characters have any development and most felt like blank slates. With that being said, the ones that were developed I adored. Lucien and Rhys saved the book for me in a lot of ways. I found them both to be complex and interesting characters. <br /><br />The last 10-15% of the book saved it for me. I found the plot to finally be interesting, and I found Feyre's decisions in those chapters to actually make sense. A lot of things were set up for future books that have me very intrigued, and I'm looking forward to the rest of the series. Many things that I disliked in this book, may in fact be remedied due to some of the occurrences in this last small section of the book. <br /><br />Overall, I was disappointed by this first installment. While there were elements I really enjoyed, they didn't make up for the elements I didn't. I'm hoping future installments will prove to be better. <br /><br />I will also be doing a full video review and spoiler-filled discussion on my <a href="http://www.youtube.com/user/thoughtsonotomes" rel="nofollow noopener">channel</a> in the future if you want to know more of my thoughts. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3696649043092043334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2004641308" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2004641308" />
    <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments"><img alt="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554228831p2/67920559.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2004641308?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰" href="/user/show/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments">Alex ✰ Comets and Comments ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=angst-with-a-capital-a">angst-with-a-capital-a</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=better-late-than-never">better-late-than-never</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=beautiful-doesnt-even-cut-it">beautiful-doesnt-even-cut-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=unlikeable-characters">unlikeable-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=2019-favorites">2019-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=cliffhanger-syndrome">cliffhanger-syndrome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/67920559-alex-comets-and-comments?shelf=family-power">family-power</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2004641308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14548409766184347972"><i>
  <b>“I wasn’t faerie, but I was a part of this earth, and the earth was a part of me, and I would be content to dance upon it for the rest of my life.”</b>
</i> <br/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653085.gif' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653086.gif' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653087.gif' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653088.gif' width='500' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b> <br/>~3.5 stars~<br/><br/>ACOTAR was nothing short of a delightful enigma, there was so much in this novel that I adored and some things that I wish were better. It blew me all the way away and left me wanting more of its glorious world and even mightier characters. <br/></b><br/>note: copyright of all fanart goes to their amazing artists<br/>_______________<br/><br/><u>
  <b>The Land of </b></u></span>
  <span id="freeText14548409766184347972" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“I wasn’t faerie, but I was a part of this earth, and the earth was a part of me, and I would be content to dance upon it for the rest of my life.”</b>
</i> <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653085.gif" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653086.gif" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653087.gif" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1560279599ra/27653088.gif" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b> <br>~3.5 stars~<br><br>ACOTAR was nothing short of a delightful enigma, there was so much in this novel that I adored and some things that I wish were better. It blew me all the way away and left me wanting more of its glorious world and even mightier characters. <br></b><br>note: copyright of all fanart goes to their amazing artists<br>_______________<br><br><u>
  <b>The Land of The Fae</b>
</u><br>So not only was this my first SJM book but it was also my first book solely based around Fae! (For the hardcore faerie fans out there, I'll send you the address of the rock I've been living under alongside an apology note.) BUT, in my defense I think this was probably the best book to start in order to both understand and learn to love the creatures. <i>Beauty and the Beast</i> has long been a Disney favourite of mine and the lush scenery as well as the lyrical writing in this novel made me swoon everytime I understood a faint reference and had me at the edge of my seat everytime it diverged from the classic tale. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> “Beauty didn’t mean anything in the forest.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i> <br><br>To be completely honest, the latter 25% of the book was a solid 4 stars for me and the beginning was bordering a 3. This was really down to the fact that I wanted <i>more</i> to happen. The pacing felt jolting at times and often I felt the storyline had assets that seemed unnecessary to the higher plot. I disliked that almost everything was revealed during the last 15% of the book. The infodump was overwhelming and I wish it had been spaced out a tad more cleverly. <br><br>Regardless, I loved the mysterious and wicked atmosphere paired with some fantastic characters and plot twists. Prythian is both dangerous and sultry, from its curses, royalty, and magical beasts. From trusted reviewers and friends, I've been advised that the second book deserves all the stars and more, so I'm definitely reading that next! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560279599i/27653089._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Characters </b>
</u><br>The characters drove the story for me, at least more than the actual plot. For once in a YA/NA fantasy novel, (this is definitely New Adult but has been advertised as Young Adult which is a controversy in itself) I liked the main heroine! Feyre was like a breath of fresh air. I enjoyed her stubbornness and maturity, I like that she made mistakes but knew where and when she was in the wrong. I also loved that she was portrayed as strong and un-doormaty... <i>Yes</i>, she has her flaws but I'm not going to complain when we finally have a 19-year old hardworking main character that believes in her values and develops through the book. <br><br>The side characters (Lucien, Rhysand and Alis) stole the show for me. My heart went out for them. I am definitely Team Rhysand but I'll get into that later ;) I felt like the dynamic between the courts and the tension from the "blight" was written really well. I followed with the backstory and the history of Prythian throughout the novel and I honestly fell for each character's story arc. Lucien has a heart of gold and Rhysand is a walking, talking stick of ego that somehow has something soft within him. Alis was my own Mrs. Potts, with her charm and blunt personality and I never felt like any of the chapters that they were in were filler chapters. Towards the end, I started getting giddy whenever Rhysand was in a chapter... (Tamlin is very irrelevant to me... but I've got a whole ass section for him coming) <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Can faeries be friends with mortals?”<br>“Five hundred years ago, enough faeries were friends with mortals that they went to war on their behalf.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560280698i/27653162._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>One of the only parts that actually made me tear up slightly was a scene between Nesta (Feyre's sister) and Feyre during the second-half of the story. Nesta seems like she's going to have the biggest character development arc and I am here for it. Lil' cold-hearted ice queen is ready to be thawed out! <br><br><br><u>
  <b>The Romance </b>
</u><br>I dislike Tamlin. <br><br>There are so many reviews that I have read now and posts where people have mocked themselves for liking Tamlin in the beginning and I kinda feel left out. But no. From the minute Feyre was held captive in his manor, there was something about his character that I couldn't settle with. He was unnerving and uncomfortable in his scenes. Some of his dialogue between Feyre and him had me cringing at the lack of chemistry. So, I can't tell you how relieved I was when I felt sparks between Rhysand and Feyre. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1560280698i/27653163._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Throughout the novel, my experience with the romance was dull. It felt forced and alarming at times. Tamlin was also the only character I felt that had no true personality... I wanted to go with the whole "captor with a heart, knight in shining armor" vibe that the story was trying to go for but I just felt like this man was taking advantage of the entire situation. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[He does. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“It took me a long while to realize that Rhysand, whether he knew it or not, had effectively kept me from shattering completely.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>Don't get me wrong, the situation with Rhysand and Feyre echoes shades of romanticized trickery as well, (I see this as a little bit of a dark romance that hopefully blooms in the next book) but I enjoyed that Feyre stuck to her own during her time Under The Mountain. I was actually quite sad when this book ended because it felt like I finished a journey in this new world. I'm so ready for ACOMAF, it's actually embarrassing at this point. <br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>““Why are you here, then?”<br>The man’s remarkable eyes seemed to glow—with enough of a deadly edge that I backed up a step. “Because all the monsters have been let out of their cages tonight, no matter what court they belong to. So I may roam wherever I wish until the dawn.””</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Pre-review </b>
</u> <br>your girl is finally bracing her first SJM book... i was promised that my crops would be thriving, my skin would be clear, my vision would be 20/20 and my heart would be full. i expect nothing less. <br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559577170i/27612665._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1559577170i/27612666._SY540_.png" width="500" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br> <br><a href="https://librariedits.tumblr.com/post/185317916241/acotar-lockscreens-like-or-reblog-if-you-save" rel="nofollow noopener">©</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14548409766184347972" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283870513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2693952622372255387">This is definitely one of my favorite books of 2015! <br/>I am a huge Beauty and the Beast fan and was in the mood for fantasy, so those combined and written by one of my favorite authors was perfection! <br/>I definitely recommend this book to everyone and can't wait for the next installment. </span>

<div id="review_1314524050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1314524050" />
    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1314524050?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake?shelf=apocalyptic-or-dystopian">apocalyptic-or-dystopian</a>,
