        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314524050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8238729267254181782"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Once again, I find myself the odd man out when it comes to a massively popular book...<br/><br/>I went into this really excited and and <i>really</i> wanting to love this thing. <br/><br/>After seeing this book and its successors paint my feed with its courts and thorns and wings and ruin, I knew there was a lot of hype surrounding this series in general.<br/><br/>And this first installment just didn't live up to it for me, sadly. <br/><br/>There, there, Court Thornians...<br/><br/> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499275224ra/23212108.gif' width='500' height='227' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Quite frankly, the first 60% of this book dragged like a U-H</span>
  <span id="freeText8238729267254181782" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br><br>Once again, I find myself the odd man out when it comes to a massively popular book...<br><br>I went into this really excited and and <i>really</i> wanting to love this thing. <br><br>After seeing this book and its successors paint my feed with its courts and thorns and wings and ruin, I knew there was a lot of hype surrounding this series in general.<br><br>And this first installment just didn't live up to it for me, sadly. <br><br>There, there, Court Thornians...<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1499275224ra/23212108.gif" width="500" height="227" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Quite frankly, the first 60% of this book dragged like a U-Haul trailer with no wheels. <br><br>Nothing really happened and the things that did didn't even make sense until after the book was over. <br><br>And I'm just not a fan of that. I like to enjoy books <i>while</i> I'm reading them, not only for the last 25-35% when everything that was murky throughout the whole book becomes clear. <br><br>I also found myself WAY more interested in Rhysand than the actual love interest, Tamlin. Whoops!<br><br>THAT SAID.<br><br>I <i>did</i> enjoy the writing and the ending.<br><br>And while those things aren't enough to prompt me to rate this thing any higher, <b>I AM going to read the second book</b>. <br><br>I trust my peeps and all of you are saying that, while the first book drags, the second book is "OMG amazeballs." And I have faith in ya'll.<br><br>Plus, I am getting it free from the library, so why not, no?<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1475857626ra/20775760.gif" width="375" height="211.5" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2047885093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047885093" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047885093?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047885093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12777046530091628624"><i>”You murdered my friend,” the beast snarled. “Murdered him, skinned his corpse, sold it at the market, and then said he deserved it, and yet you have the nerve to question my generosity?”</i><br/><br/>When I first read <b>“A Court of Thorns and Roses”</b> I thought that this would be some sort of “The Beauty and the Beast” retelling and I guess in some way it truly is. Well, at least at first it seems to be one, the longer you read, the more it goes into an entirely different direction though.<br/><br/>And I think it was exac</span>
  <span id="freeText12777046530091628624" style="display:none"><i>”You murdered my friend,” the beast snarled. “Murdered him, skinned his corpse, sold it at the market, and then said he deserved it, and yet you have the nerve to question my generosity?”</i><br /><br />When I first read <b>“A Court of Thorns and Roses”</b> I thought that this would be some sort of “The Beauty and the Beast” retelling and I guess in some way it truly is. Well, at least at first it seems to be one, the longer you read, the more it goes into an entirely different direction though.<br /><br />And I think it was exactly that kind of change of direction that actually got me hooked in the end. I mean I like “The Beauty and the Beast” stories but boy, did I live and breathe for this story that didn’t only feature faeries but also magic and cruel villains! So yes, when I first read ACOTAR I got lost in its universe and rushed through it, always eager to find out more and to continue with Feyre’s journey.<br /><br />It was only after I finished the last book, that I realized how fast I’d been paging through the entire series and by then it was already too late to savour it properly. Needless to say that I was sad it was over, also needless to say that I wanted to do a reread of it one day. *lol*<br /><br />So two years later I found myself sitting down with ACOTAR once again, and tell you what? It was even better this second time around! It was so damn good to read about my favourite characters and it almost felt like coming home! Plus the foreboding!!! Seriously, how did I even miss all those clues and hints when I read it for the very first time?! There were so many things that made a whole lot more sense than they did before and I was in awe at how well Sarah J. Maas wove all those details in her storyline. Also the ending! I’ll never get over that ending!<br /><br /><u>
  <b>NEVER!</b>
</u><br /><br />No matter how often I read this book that moment on the last page!? Wow, just wow! T_T<br />This said I enjoyed this reread immensely and I really can’t wait to continue with ACOMAF soon! It was my favourite book out of this series and I’m sure I’ll find even more interesting details when I read it again! XD<br /><br />Well, enough of my impending future reread! Let’s head to my character section instead! ;-)<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>You are now entering Prythian and if you decide to continue your journey into the Spring Court you’ll be gifted with thousands and thousands of spoilers and thorns! Believe me and take my word for it. I mean faeries can’t lie and always tell the truth, right? ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Feyre:</b><br /><br /><i>”Because I wouldn’t want to die alone,” I said, and my voice wobbled as I looked at Tamlin again, forcing myself to meet his stare. “Because I’d want someone to hold my hand until the end, and awhile after that. That’s something everyone deserves, human or faerie.”</i><br /><br />Wow, I totally forgot how much I liked Feyre at the beginning of this series. I loved that fierce girl that would do everything for her loved ones and even had the guts to kill a wolf she suspected to be a faerie! XD I mean she didn’t know for certain but it definitely didn’t stop her from shooting that fateful arrow! Still, considering how her family treated her I can’t help but think that she’s a saint! She tried to keep them alive and all they did was to sneer at her or to spend all the precious money she earned. No wonder that girl is so insecure and distrustful, no wonder she was afraid of Tamlin and Lucien. No matter how scared she was, she never let it get in her way though. Her fear didn’t paralyze her but drove her and I loved that about her character! &lt;3 Plus she’s shrewd and clever! And defiant! Did I already mention how much I adore her for that? So yes, I loved the Feyre of book one and I’m kinda curious how I’ll feel about her in book two. <br /><br /><i>”I took a few running steps and hurled the bone at her with all my remaining strength. It embedded itself in the mud at her feet, splattering filth onto her white gown, and remained there, quivering.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Kill a faerie, fall in love with a faerie, then be forced to kill a faerie to keep that love. It was brilliant and cruel, and she knew it.”</i><br /><br /><i>”You went after me,” I said. “You went after me – to Prythian.”<br />“I got to the wall. I couldn’t find a way through.”<br />I raised a shaking hand to my throat. “You trekked two days there and two days back – through the winter woods?”</i> <br /><br /><b>Tamlin:</b><br /><br /><i>”I was a child at the time, too young to understand what was happening – or even to be told,” he said. A child. Which meant he had to be over… “But had I been old enough, I would have. Against slavery, against tyranny, I would gladly go to my death, no matter whose freedom I was defending.”</i><br /><br /><b>LIAR, LIAR, PANTS ON FIRE!!!</b> URGH! I can’t say how sick this moment made me! Seriously, when I read the book for the very first time I actually believed him, but damn reading it for a second time I realized how stupid I was. I mean for some reason I was never happy with Tamlin as a love interest for Feyre, not even when I read ACOTAR for the first time, I could never pinpoint the reason for it though. XD Oh well, I certainly don’t have that problem anymore. Doing a reread of this book I finally realized the many things I never truly liked about him. For instance his cold distance, his controlling behaviour and how he could say sentences like the one above when every freaking Court of Prythian except of his own was enslaved to Amarantha! He was old enough to fight her now but he was still indifferent!! All those other High Lords felt lonely too, Tamlin! They hoped that you would break the curse! And boy, I bet they had way worse days than you over those last fifty years!!!!They freaking DAMN WELL KNOW how it feels to care for their people when they are slaughtered and tortured in front of them!!! ADKFLASKDFSAKADKSK! So NOPE! Just nope! I get that he had a lot of weight on his shoulders, I get that he felt lonely, I get that he didn’t want Feyre to die, but he should have tried to do something. To manipulate Amarantha. I mean he didn’t even try that. He just flat out refused her! Which is stupid on so many levels…. Anyway I could go on and on but I’ll leave it at that! #I’llNeverBeAFanOfTamlin and I stand by it. <br /><br /><i>”But they never understood. What it was like, what it is like, for me to care for my people, my lands. What scars are still there, what the bad days feel like.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Lucien:</b><br /><br /><i>”In lieu of a pretty breakfast table by the window, a worn worktable dominated the space, covered in various weapons. It was there he sat, wearing only a white shirt and trousers, his red hair unbound and gleaming like liquid fire. Tamlin’s court-trained emissary, but a warrior in his own right.”</i><br /><br /><br /><b>LUCIEN!!!</b> My precious tender autumn leave!!! Gosh, I love him even more after rereading ACOTAR! &lt;333 This man is honourable and strong and a true friend and no matter what others think about him, I still believe that he’s amazing! I’ll never understand why he gets so much hate from the fans because let’s face it, aside from Rhys he was Feyre’s only true friend!! He’s always honest and he says exactly what he thinks! Even if it’s to his detriment like when he told Amarantha to go back to her shit-hole! In contrast to Tamlin he had the guts to stand up to Amarantha and yes, he paid dearly for it, but he gave her a piece of his mind and I think Feyre and him are quite similar in that regard. *lol* AND this boy has compassion, fire and snark! Plus he’s a faithful soul! If you ask me he’s way more attractive than Tamlin and I for my part would love nothing more than to get burned by those hot autumn flames. *wriggles eyebrows* *LOL* I just hope Sarah won’t ruin him even more in the books that follow after the ACOTAR series because he definitely deserves better than that!! &lt;333 You hear me, Sarah? Please give my boy a Happy Ever After! <br /><br /><i>”I heard you scream,” he said as I examined the blade in my hands. I’d never held one so finely crafted, so perfectly balanced. “And I hesitated. Not long, but I hesitated before I came running. Even though Tam got there in time, I still broke my word in those seconds I waited.” He jerked his chin at the knife. “It’s yours. Don’t bury it in my back, please.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Lucien told her to go back to the shit-hole she’d crawled out of. She took his eye as punishment. Carved it out with her own fingernail, then scarred his face. She sent him back so bloody that Tamlin… The High Lord vomited when he saw his friend.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I risked my neck for you during your task. Was that not enough?” His metal eye whirred softly. “You offered up your name for me – after all that I said to you, all I did, you still offered up your name. Didn’t you realize I would help you after that? Oath or no oath?”</i><br /><br /><b>Rhysand:</b><br /><br /><i>”I stepped out of the shelter of my saviour’s arm and turned to thank him.<br />Standing before me was the most beautiful man I’d ever seen.”</i><br /><br />Ohhh Rhys! Haha! Next to Lucien he was definitely my second favourite character of this book! I already loved him when I read ACOTAR for the first time and nothing changed. I know so many people were angry at him for using Feyre and even more of them said that he’s an asshole, but what can I say? I like dark, mysterious, assholes? *LOL* When everyone was charmed by Tamlin and despised Rhys, he had already won my heart. XD And seriously, if you read the book carefully you can see through his disguise. Ironically Tamlin is the one wearing the obvious mask but in fact it’s Rhys who’s hiding behind one. Which only makes him even more lovable because every now and then it slips and we’re able to see the true High Lord! Behind that cunning and cruel mind there is a very decent person and everyone who doesn’t see this is blinded by Tamlin’s white teeth! *lol* Just saying! XD I mean even Feyre noticed that there’s more behind Rhys actions and half of the time she was severely wounded, having a fever or under the influence of drugs! XD So yeah! I love that scheming mind and I can’t wait to see more of it in ACOMAF! <br /><br /><i>”His clothes – all black, all finely made – were cut close enough to his body that I could see how magnificent he was. As if he’d been molded from the night itself.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Because,” he went on, his eyes locked with mine. “I didn’t want you to fight alone. Or die alone.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Be glad of your human heart, Feyre. Pity those who don’t feel anything at all.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Feyre &amp; Tamlin:</u><br /><br /><i>”You gave up so much for them.” He lifted his other hand as if to brush my cheek. I braced myself for the touch, but he lowered it before making contact. “Do you ever know how to laugh?”</i><br /><br />I didn’t feel this romance… at all! I already didn’t feel it when I read ACOTAR for the first time and I didn’t now. Those two just don’t have any chemistry! Their sweet moments weren’t even exciting or anything, but then again I think that this might have been Sarah’s intention all along. I dunno what it is about Sarah but you know exactly when she wants a couple to be endgame, because damn, their chemistry is always off the charts. If the couple isn’t going to have a HEA you can read it in the way she writes their sexy moments and sweet scenes. XD Or maybe it’s just my imagination? *lol* Anyway, I guess I was supposed to like them as a couple and to ship them, but I somehow never did? Plus I think their relationship never had a chance to develop. It was from “I hate you” to “I accept you” and then they were suddenly in love. I guess from Feyre’s POV it made sense, she’s young and unexperienced and Tamlin was the first guy who was nice to her and her first love. I somehow never felt that dedication from Tamlin though. Yes, he tried to save her but to be fascinated by her is no real love. To me it sounded like she was something pretty he wanted to possess and that just didn’t work for me. #SorryNotSorry<br /><br /><i>”Because your human joy fascinates me – the way you experience things, in your life span, so wildly and deeply and all at once, is … entrancing. I’m drawn to it, even when I know I shouldn’t be, even when I try not to be.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Stay with the High Lord, human,” the Suriel said.</i><br /><br /><u>Feyre &amp; Lucien:</u><br /><br /><i>Lucien went rigid, but he hopped off the edge of the table and bowed deeply to me. ”My apologies, lady.” Another joke at my expense. “I’m Lucien. Courtier and emissary.” He gestured to me with a flourish. “Your eyes are like stars, and your hair like burnished gold.”</i><br /><br />I absolutely love and adore their friendship! I mean they start out as enemies. Feyre killed Andras and as it seems Lucien was pretty close to the sentinel so it’s understandable that he’s not only angry but also dislikes her at first. During the entire book they get to know each other better though and slowly but gradually they become friends in the end. XD At first it seems to be some sort of reluctant acceptance and acknowledgement but the longer they talk to each other the better their relationship becomes. =) And let me tell you this: They are friendship goals! There’s nothing they wouldn’t do for each other! &lt;333 Feyre saved Lucien by giving Amarantha her name and Lucien risked everything when he healed her nose, gave her a cloak and shouted that warning at her trial! He got a lashing just for telling her where to look and if that isn’t true friendship I dunno! Plus they work so nicely together, their easy banter is hilarious and I’m glad Lucien finally found someone who’s able to keep up with him. *lol* So yes, I’m on board of this friend-ship and I love them together! <br /><br /><i>Lucien sighed as he looked me over. “Do you ever stop being so serious and dull?”<br />“Do you ever stop being such a prick?” I snapped back.<br />Dead – really, truly, I should have been dead for that.<br />But Lucien grinned at me. “Much better.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Faerie pig!” I yelled, and Lucien howled, almost tipping back in his chair. At the sight of Tamlin’s growing smile, I left.</i><br /><br /><i>He used the dagger to clean his nails. “I’ve been busy. So have you, I take it.”<br />“What’s that supposed to mean?” I demanded.<br />“If I offer you the moon on a string, will you give me a kiss, too?”</i><br /><br /><i>Downstairs, Lucien snorted at the sight of me. “Those clothes are enough to convince me I never want to enter the human realm.”<br />“I’m not sure the human realm would know what to do with you,” I said.</i> <br /><br /><u>Feyre &amp; Rhysand:</u><br /><br /><i>”You’re going to bargain?” Rhysand laughed under his breath. “Ten days.”<br />I held his stare with all my strength. “A week.”<br />Rhysand was silent for a long moment, his eyes traveling across my body and my face before he murmured: “A week it is.”</i><br /><br />Okay, let me tell you this: If you didn’t notice that Rhys has a weakness for Feyre you most certainly read the book with tomatoes on your eyes. *LOL* Because no offence, but it’s obvious and plain as day! He basically protected her from the moment they first met at Calanmai and there was absolutely no reason for him to interfere! She was just a human and he’s a High Faerie, yet he stepped in KNOWING full well that Tamlin and Feyre had something going on! Calanmai was the first time he was intrigued by her and he could have easily rat her out right after that night. He didn’t though. In fact everything he did was to protect her! He protected her the moment she came to Under the Mountain and everything he did, even the colour on her body, had some reason behind it. None of his actions was arbitrary, every single move and gesture was deliberate and on purpose. And if you still don’t believe me then think about the final fight against Amarantha! Rhys was the only one who tried to stop her! He raised his hand against Amarantha because he WANTED to save Feyre and he didn’t even think about himself when he attacked her! And don’t even get me talking about the fact that Rhys stumbled, ACTUALLY STUMBLED, in the end!!! &lt;333 I ship them! Period! XD<br /><br /><i>”Don’t let her see you cry.<br />Put your hands at your sides and stand up.<br />I couldn’t. I couldn’t move.<br />Stand. Don’t give her the satisfaction of seeing you break.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Why are you telling me this?”<br />The swagger and nastiness were gone. “Because I’m tired and lonely, and you’re the only person I can talk to without putting myself at risk.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Then Rhysand was on his feet, my bloody knife in his hands. He launched himself at Amarantha, swift as a shadow, the ash dagger aimed at her throat.”</i><br /><br /><i>”His eyes locked on mine, wide and wild, and his nostrils flared. Shock – pure shock flashed across his features at whatever he saw on my face, and he stumbled back a step. Actually, stumbled.”</i><br /><br /> <b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />If you love faerie stories and like your faeries dark, dangerous, intriguing, silver-tongued and sexy as hell then this is certainly the right book for you. Sarah J. Maas outdid herself with the ACOTAR series and this was only the start! There’s so much more to come and to look forward to and I can’t wait to reread ACOMAF and ACOWAR! If you still haven’t read this book you definitely should go and grab a copy of it. You don’t have to be a “The Beauty and the Beast” fan to read it, just start with the first page and see where it will lead you! I promise it will be an interesting journey! ;-P<br />___________________________________<br /><br />PREREVIEW:<br /><br />*rolls up sleeves*<br />I’m finally rereading ACOTAR and I can’t wait to dive back into this world!! <br />I missed all those characters so much and every time I saw an update or a review I longed to read it again. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />So here I am! <br />Ready to reread one of my faves! And this time around there will even be a proper review! <br />My “goodreads me” would never forgive my “pre-goodreads me” if I wouldn’t write one. *lol*<br /><br />Also: I might love all of those characters, but if you know me, you know which boy I want to read about the most! &lt;333<br /><br /><b>LUCIEN VANSERRA!</b> <br />My precious sarcastic red-head! ;-P<br />I’m coming! &lt;333<br /><br />P.S: I'm curious if my rating is going to change! *lol*</span>
  <a data-text-id="12777046530091628624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1085674516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1085674516" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1085674516?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085674516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4683779942829515049">SARAH J MAAS DOES IT AGAIN!!!! KNOCKED MY FREAKING SOCKS OFF AND WITH A STORY RE-TELLING?!!!!<br/><br/>I <b>hate </b>story re-tellings!!! I hate them but this, this master piece is no <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>. I'm just gonna jump right into everything and just a little warning: I'm so sorry if this seems like I'm frantically flapping around on my keyboard, but I'm just that excited. <br/><br/>I was so worried that this book would have a plot too close to <i>Throne of Glass</i> and that the characters would also bare that same fate..</span>
  <span id="freeText4683779942829515049" style="display:none">SARAH J MAAS DOES IT AGAIN!!!! KNOCKED MY FREAKING SOCKS OFF AND WITH A STORY RE-TELLING?!!!!<br><br>I <b>hate </b>story re-tellings!!! I hate them but this, this master piece is no <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>. I'm just gonna jump right into everything and just a little warning: I'm so sorry if this seems like I'm frantically flapping around on my keyboard, but I'm just that excited. <br><br>I was so worried that this book would have a plot too close to <i>Throne of Glass</i> and that the characters would also bare that same fate... But thank the literary gods above that didn't happen. Yes, Maas still gives us swoon worthy gents and a strong leading fem, but they are not at all like the cast of <i>ToG</i>. Our leading lass is Feyre, and man oh man did I love her. I loved that though she is strong she isn't doing it for herself or because that's who she is, she's doing to because it's what needs to be done. This is what made her character for me. She does everything for everyone and expects nothing in return. Her character starts as a strong huntress and turns into something more. She has the head strong will of a warrior and the heart of an artist. I loved that Maas gave her so much depth and let us get so deep into her brain that her feelings become your feelings. As for Feyre's love interested she gives us the heart twist-swoon worthy-deep-thoughtful-man candy that is Tamlin. Oh Tamlin will have you weak in the knees and have your loins aflame (seriously blushed so much during this book). He literately has so much weight on his shoulders and still stands tall. He is willing to give up everything to make sure shes okay. <b>I kid y'all not I never ever use the word "ship" for couples, but as they say there's a first for everything and.... I SHIP THEM!!! I SHIP THEM SO HARD! YOU SEE THAT SPOT OVER THERE IN THE DISTANCE THAT IS THEIR SHIP AND IT IS SAILING!!! </b><br><br><div>
<br><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-TeNGRKrCZKg/VVKAWWbsKrI/AAAAAAAABp4/8Hn9HLKc8cI/s1600/ship.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="128" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431470781ra/14839721.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div><br><br>Can't stress enough how much I loved their relationship. I love that this book is based around it and its growth. They have such a push and pull. I love that one has everything and one is holding on to anything. How they play off each other is so well written. Also had my brain rocked by how Maas stepped up her sexy game in this book... Because its like a sauna in there! Whoosh so good! *Round of applause* .The sub characters like the rest of the story are so well done. Lucien, Tam's best friend, has got to be one of my favorites in this book. His loyalty won me over. Plus he isn't so bad on the eyes if ya get what I mean... At one point I even remember saying "<i>I don't know who I like more Teen Wolf or the Sexy Fox with one eye"</i>... Yeah, Maas makes having one eye even sound hot! The evil Queen in this book was the perfect amount of mystery and you will hate her. And then there's Rhysand... There's not much I'll say about him, but what I will say is that even when Maas gives you characters you're suppose to hate you still end up falling in love with them.<br><br><i>“Be glad of your human heart, Feyre. Pity those who don’t feel anything at all.” </i><br><br>The plot and world building in this book are so beyond what a lot of other authors would have given us. There are so many vivid details, so many beautifully painted scenes, and so many perfectly peeled layers. I was never once left to question what the world looked like (or characters), and I was thankful for this. Sometimes I do like to fill in the holes with my own ideas but not when it comes to high fantasy reads like this one. The plot is action packed. We have this heavy start to the book, a world building middle, and a jam slammed action packed ending. <b>Because let me tell you when everything comes together and everything is slowly shown you will be tossing your book in the air or punching your kindles in their faces... You will freak out!</b> It's like the end scene to <i>Inception </i>where that heavy DOM DOM music starts playing and the dream is collapsing and everything just falls together for this epic ending! Even the things you know are coming will still rock you to your bones. Maas gives you this heart filled, gut wrenching, wtf ending that I myself couldn't of been happier about. I ate this story up!!!! The plot is just as strong as the characters, and I'm so glad this wasn't a let down. Maas perfectly blends both the YA and NA worlds into this one book. This is a book that will make your heart race and make you want to lose those precise few hours of sleep just to snag a few more chapters... And it'll be worth it too!<br><br><b>A Court of Thorns and Roses was the tits.<br><br><b> Read this review and others over on my blog<br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><a href="http://betweenthesheetsandcovers.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the sheets &amp; covers blog</a> <br><br>Originally read April 2015 <br>Re-read April 2016</b></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4683779942829515049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2732260582" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2732260582" />
    <a title="Cindy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy"><img alt="Cindy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598112512p2/57797254.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2732260582?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy" href="/user/show/57797254-cindy">Cindy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2732260582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5937857381089504079">I approached this book with an open mind and wanted to enjoy it. Despite not being a fan of the superfluous writing style or the lackluster world-building, I was still willing to rate it 3 stars by viewing it as an easy guilty pleasure romance book. The relationship seems harmless and I still don't see how it's as problematic as people dramatize it to be. The first half of the book is a standard Beauty and the Beast retelling — not awful, but not special either — and then the second half really </span>
  <span id="freeText5937857381089504079" style="display:none">I approached this book with an open mind and wanted to enjoy it. Despite not being a fan of the superfluous writing style or the lackluster world-building, I was still willing to rate it 3 stars by viewing it as an easy guilty pleasure romance book. The relationship seems harmless and I still don't see how it's as problematic as people dramatize it to be. The first half of the book is a standard Beauty and the Beast retelling — not awful, but not special either — and then the second half really dips in quality, which lowered my rating to 2 stars. <br /><br />A couple glaring issues that stood out to me:<br /><br />1) The background story of the curse is literally told instead of shown via a side character's lengthy monologue. This was disappointing since I was intrigued to find this out by piecing clues together, not by being told it straightforwardly like a regurgitated wikipedia article.<br /><br />2) The main character seems relatively smart but consistently has leaps of logic that are clearly there for the sake of plot. 9 out of 10 times she won't follow the advice of another character.<br /><br />3) The antagonist is SO cartoonish — like mustache-twirling cartoonish. She gives a bunch of arbitrary challenges and rules for no reason other than for the sake of stringing along a story. It feels like she's hosting a game show or some overly complex scavenger hunt. There's no reason why she'd bother setting up any of these superfluous rules. I think this is the worst antagonist I've ever read.<br /><br />I'm willing to overlook the writing style and bland romance, but once I got to the part where Feyre answers the riddle, I had to drop it down to 2 stars because it was so ridiculous and lazy. I've heard that the sequel is much better though, so I am willing to give it another try, just not any time soon haha.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5937857381089504079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15909565902107863321" style="display:none"><b>UPDATE: $1.99 on Kindle US today 12/23/18</b><br /><br />This was a re-read on Audible. It's my favorite new thing, to re-read books either through Audible or Overdrive. <br /><br />I must say this was better the second time around but ye gods, I thought I was going to gag a maggot with all the lovey dovey and sex with Tamlin. I mean after falling in love with Rhys I can't even people. And also, who could have sex with some old beast after he had that ritual thing with someone else. Ewwww! I know it's some THING but I don't give a rats arse! Anyhoo, on to the next! <br /><br />Mel ❤️<br /><br /><br />*****Old Review*****<br /><br />I had a love/hate relationship with this book. I loved it so much in the beginning, then I felt a little off with it for a bit, but the end took me right back to loving it. <br /><br />I think this is a very unique take on Beauty and the Beast. I loved Tamlin, but I wonder! There were times that Feyre got on my last nerves and I wanted to smack her, but it happens. She did great over all. <br /><br />I loved some of the characters in the book. There is Lucien, who I hope to learn more about in the next book. Alis, who is Feyre's sort of maiden when she comes to the manor. And I actually liked Rhysand in the end. He's a bad guy of sorts but I won't give that spoiler away. I just want more of him! <br /><br />I loved the scenery I pictured in the book from the descriptions. It seems like a beautiful place to live, or is it? There is all sorts of bad stuff going on, bad monsters, curses, killings, you know, the normal stuff! <br /><br />I'm not sure where the next book is going to take us, but there was something a little weird happen at the end and I'm hoping that is explained. <br /><br />This is not a HUGE action book, but I think it's coming! <br /><br />I can't wait!! <br /><br />Mel ❤️</span>

<div id="review_472884462" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472884462" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472884462?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/23666139-a-court-of-thorns-and-roses">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Lovers of fantasy, Fae, and fairy tale retellings.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=creeptastic">creeptastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=sestras">sestras</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=diabolical">diabolical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorite-secondary-characters">favorite-secondary-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=matchy-matchy">matchy-matchy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472884462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18109341117106219051"><b>5/3/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b><br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://amzn.to/2HNCfG3'>https://amzn.to/2HNCfG3</a><br/><br/><b>4/17/18:</b> Maybe it’s b/c I listened to it—the narrator was fantastic—but Feyre was a lot less irritating this time around. Then there’s the fact that I already knew <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[Tamlin is NOT a good guy. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I took almost sadistic pleasure in cataloguing all the signs, and, MAN ALIVE, there were a lot of them.<br/><br/>And all of that is why I’m raising my original 3.5 star rating to a full 4.0 stars. #idowhatiwant<br/><br/><b>4/16/18:</b> REREAD. B/c finally </span>
  <span id="freeText18109341117106219051" style="display:none"><b>5/3/18 - ON SALE for $2.99:</b><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://amzn.to/2HNCfG3">https://amzn.to/2HNCfG3</a><br><br><b>4/17/18:</b> Maybe it’s b/c I listened to it—the narrator was fantastic—but Feyre was a lot less irritating this time around. Then there’s the fact that I already knew <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tamlin is NOT a good guy. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I took almost sadistic pleasure in cataloguing all the signs, and, MAN ALIVE, there were a lot of them.<br><br>And all of that is why I’m raising my original 3.5 star rating to a full 4.0 stars. #idowhatiwant<br><br><b>4/16/18:</b> REREAD. B/c finally going to finish #3 in preparation for ACOFAS (which is less than 300 pages, FYI). 😱<br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/05/review-a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-by-sarah-j-maas.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>Where to begin . . . <br><br>A COURT OF THORNS AND ROSES was and <em>wasn’t</em> exactly what I was expecting. <br><br>I knew it was going to be a sort of <em>Beauty and the Beast</em> meets <em>Tamlin</em> mashup . . . but I didn’t really think about what that might mean.<br><br>When I think of retellings, especially fairy tale retellings, I think of the Brothers Grimm and Hans Christian Anderson. I think of folk stories and mythologies that have no author to speak of, b/c they’re part of an oral tradition that no single person can lay claim to. <br><br>What I do <em>not</em> think of is Disney. <br><br>Disney is the end product of a retelling. It’s not whence the retelling came. So . . . in my mind . . . a retelling of anything Disney . . . is a <em>retelling</em> of a retelling. And while the <em>Beauty and the Beast</em> portion of our story wasn't entirely Disney, it <em>was</em> significantly Disney.<br><br>So here's the deal: I liked this book. I really did, and cumulatively I have zero apprehensions about recommending it to fellow lovers of fantasy and fairy tale retellings . . . <br><br>BUT. I also had a lot of tiny issues that combined to be less tiny, in addition to an issue that by itself wasn't tiny at all . . . <br><br>So. Tiny things (the "<em>she</em>"s and "<em>her</em>"s are b/c we didn't get a name for a long, long time):<br><br><b>1. The masks</b> that Tamlin and all the members of his house have stuck to their faces . . . <br><br>I thought they were both unnecessary and . . . a little bit silly.<br><br>We're told that they're the result of <i>her</i> lashing out in anger . . . okaaaaay . . . hmm . . . Was there seriously no one else who thought, "Oh no! Not masks, anything but masks!"? <br><br>That's the silly part. <br><br>The unnecessary part is that Tamlin has a beast form. If <i>she</i> was really concerned about making it more difficult for him to do-the-thing, maybe it's just me, but in a retelling of <i>Beauty and the</i> freaking <i>Beast</i>, wouldn't it make more sense to, oh, I don't know, trap him as a BEAST? <br><br><b>2. As much as it pains me to say it, there was a some redundancy</b> (and this is actually three separate tiny things):<br><br>In the beginning, if Feyre wasn't trying to escape, b/c, yes, <em>we know</em>, she made a promise, she was blithely walking into traps that the teensiest bit of foresight could have prevented. <br><br>In the aftermath of her inevitable rescues, her reaction was always some variation of, "I'm a stupid, insignificant peasant, and I'm even more stupid and peasant-like for forgetting that I'm a stupid, insignificant peasant." <br><br>And I have a lot of sympathy for Feyre, I really do. Not being able to do-the-thing would give me a complex too. But that complex was made an issue too frequently, and the resulting tantrums got tiresome.<br><br>When Tamlin feels compelled to premeditatedly say, "Before you start yelling . . .," it's a problem.<br><br><b>Not-so-tiny thing:</b><br><br>Just to be safe, I'm spoiler tagging this. It's not much of a spoiler, but it is a piece of information that isn't revealed until you're well into the book:<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Having fae that can lie is like having vampires that don't drink blood or werewolves that don't change on the full moon.<br><br>If you don't see the problem with that, then this won't bother you, but guys . . . we're talking about my FAEvorite group of supernaturals. There are reasons I prefer Fae above all others, and one of the biggest is that THEY CANNOT LIE. <br><br>It's a double-edged sword. <br><br>On the one hand, if you can force them to speak in a way that leaves no room for misinterpretation, then you can take comfort in the truth. On the other hand, can you ever be absolutely sure you've outwitted a fae?<br><br>It's tricksy and uncertain and leaves immeasurable room for a clever author to mislead and beguile you, and I LOVE it.<br><br>And so . . . words cannot express my intractability on the subject of fae being <i>able</i> to lie. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>So not a perfect book. But I still liked it. <br><br>If you think beast-form is smelly with poor table manners and masks are an excellent alternative, or that my idea of redundancy is really determination, then you will <i>more than like</i> this book. I can't imagine that many people are as hardcore about FAE as I am, so I'm not even going to pretend that might be an issue for you, and I have no one to blame but myself for going into it with preconceived notions about what it means to be a "retelling." <br><br>And despite those notions, there was a lot of legitimate Fae lore. <br><br>Then there's--what for me was--the book's crowning glory: Feyre's relationship with her family. You will be shocked with how everything eventually plays out, and I'm talking about the good kind of shock. The kind of shock that fills you so full of warmth that you're half convinced you glow with it.<br><br>ALSO no cliffhanger. <br><br>So. Time to find out for yourself. A COURT OF THORNS AND ROSES is a fantastical (re)retelling of a beloved classic and an older, lesser known folktale from the British Isles, combining both into something completely new. With a tortured hero trying to protect his people from an evil would-be queen, Evil Queen's enforcer whose real intent is as easy to discern as a path back to civilization in a dark, unfamiliar forest, and the girl who shines like a beacon and may just save them all, this is a book that will appeal to a broad demographic. Recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>My other reviews for this series:</b><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192308232" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #2)</a>
</b><br><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436854277" rel="nofollow noopener">Untitled (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #3)</a>
</b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

    <a title="Mary S. R." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r"><img alt="Mary S. R." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597037601p2/75831724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2569180083?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary S. R." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary S. R." href="/user/show/75831724-mary-s-r">Mary S. R.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/75831724-mary-s-r?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569180083" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6088886745972765366">(<b>3.5 ★’s</b>)<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Be glad of your human heart, Feyre. Pity those who don’t feel anything at all.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>As a fairytalish, charming, and romantic retelling of <b>
  <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>
</b> mixed with the Scottish ballad of <i>Tam Lin</i>, this book is perhaps too romance-heavy for my taste even as it stays true to the style of both its inspirations, all while delivering a much appreciated and fresh look at the timeless tale of B&tB. What fresh look, you wonder? Check the <i>
  <b>Relationships</b>
</i> section for that.<br/><br/><b>Deciding on a</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6088886745972765366" style="display:none">(<b>3.5 ★’s</b>)<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Be glad of your human heart, Feyre. Pity those who don’t feel anything at all.”</i>
</blockquote><br>As a fairytalish, charming, and romantic retelling of <b>
  <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>
</b> mixed with the Scottish ballad of <i>Tam Lin</i>, this book is perhaps too romance-heavy for my taste even as it stays true to the style of both its inspirations, all while delivering a much appreciated and fresh look at the timeless tale of B&amp;tB. What fresh look, you wonder? Check the <i>
  <b>Relationships</b>
</i> section for that.<br><br><b>Deciding on a rating for ACoTaR makes me feel as if I’ve been told I have to pick one between dark chocolate and lavashak (<i>Persian fruit leather</i>) to have access to for the rest of my life, being denied the other for eternity.</b> It’s <i>torture</i>.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>For a moment, I wished I had it in me to feel remorse for the dead thing.<br>But this was the forest, and it was winter.</i>
</blockquote><br>The beginning chapters are absolutely magnificent, but then for a long while the book does not deliver on the promised brutality, focusing solely on a soft romance (<i>which is fine if you enjoy that, it’s B&amp;tB after all</i>). On top of that, the first two thirds are mysterious and confusing with many things which sound foolish or nonsensical and unnecessary...until they don’t. Thus, since I want both the God and the date, as we Persians like to say, I’m dividing the book into three parts to rate seperately:<br><br>First Third ➾ ★★★✯☆<br>Middle Third ➾ ★★☆☆☆<br>Last Third ➾ ★★★★★<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“We need hope as much as we need bread and meat,” he interrupted, his eyes clear for a rare moment. “We need hope, or else we cannot endure.”</i>
</blockquote><br>In true <i>Sarah J. Maas</i> fashion, this take is all about hope and a better world. I might’ve found her consistent and persistent theme cheesy if it weren’t also an endearing and, in a sense, brave way to look at life, digging your heels in against all dark and unfair twists of fate, insisting that every kindness and sacrifice will come back to you tenfold. <b>It takes courage to be an optimist.</b><br><br>But, even with the light and romantic message woven throughout the book, ACoTaR still carries a land of danger and deadly things on its shoulders, with SJM’s trademark violent animalistic faeries prowling through the pages from cover to cover. From a very faerie curse, to a riddle whose answer is more symbolic than practical, and an unstable and obsessive villain who has the tendency to sound like a baby while raving mad, to a folklorish world, <b><i>A Court of Thorns and Roses</i> truly does establish itself as a fairytale thorough and thorough.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Because all the monsters have been let out of their cages tonight, no matter what court they belong to. So I may roam wherever I wish until the dawn.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>CW</u>
</b> ➾ graphic mature content (becomes even more graphic in the sequels), graphic violence, gore, mutilation (mentioned), abuse (mentioned)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Storyline ❀</u>
</b><br><br>Feyre, the youngest of three sisters with a hopeless and broken father, has to singlehandedly keep their starving family alive by hunting in the woods close to the border between the human and faerie world in the unholiest of weathers, until she is dragged beyond the Wall and into Prythian, where danger lurks behind every bush, for the murder of a High Fae.<br><br>There, in a castle out of dreams, she grapples with her feelings morphing from hatred to passion, and finds that her captor is not all he seems and that, with the threat looming over magic and mundane alike, <b>perhaps <i>nothing</i> is as it seems.</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“So,” he said wearily, “here we are, with the fate of our immortal world in the hands of an illiterate human.”</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Storytelling ❀</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I’d sworn it to her, and then she’d died, and in our miserable human world—shielded only by the promise made by the High Fae five centuries ago—in our world where we’d forgotten the names of our gods, a promise was law; a promise was currency; a promise was your bond.</i>
</blockquote><br>By now it’s known that Maas indeed knows how to tell a story. With the touch of a weaver 0f tales, the thrill of well-written action scenes (<i>which are unfortunately few and towards the end</i>), and the craftsmanship of a true artist drowning in colours and paint, ACoTaR continues the enchanting writing style I cannot get enough of.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Characters ❀</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Love won’t feed a hungry belly,”</i>
</blockquote><br>➸ <b>
  <i>Feyre:</i>
</b> “Thorny. Prickly. Sour. Contrary.” Our protagonist is a bold, bitter, brave huntress who honestly deserves the world. She’s given everything to keep her promise to provide for her fallen family, and nothing lovely (<i>like the paint she loves to stain her hands with with, the brushes she loves to make dance across wood and wall</i>) has a place in her life anymore. <b>It made my heart ache to see her shame of her illiteracy, her fear of showing herself through her art, her indecision over what to do with a life she’s been finally been given the reins to even in captivity</b> (<i>which shows how truly caged she had been to have freedom in captivity</i>), and her letting go of caution and allowing herself to have peace even as she becomes dormant.<br><br>➸ <b>
  <i>Tamlin:</i>
</b> He is the Beast thorough and thorough. Emotional, caring, lonely, cold, defeated, melancholy. And I feel so, so sorry for him, because <i>he’s trying</i>. Trying to help, trying to do right. But he fails, because he can’t communicate; can’t talk, can’t listen, can’t understand. He is less considerate and more controlling, doing what he thinks others want and need without asking, and <i>what if he is wrong?</i> What if his assumptions and his forceful behaviour hurt rather than help? I guess we’ll see in the sequel, but I want to say that his moods and anger issues make me believe he needs serious therapy.<br><br>➸ <b>
  <i>Rhysand:</i>
</b> Cauldron boil and fry me, this charming, wicked, mysterious dude had my attention by the throat from the moment he said “Th—”. Yes, he is using and even violating the MC in parts even as he unexpectedly helps her, and it’s not <i>right</i> to treat another person this way, but desperate times call for desperate measures and his questionable choices are not glossed over.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Do you lie awake at night to come up with all your witty replies for the following day?”</i>
</blockquote><br>➸ <b>
  <i>Lucien:</i>
</b> Seriously, who is even surprised that I enjoyed this court-trained and mischievous yet vulnerable and caring fox? I admit, the reread made me appreciate him more, but how could I possibly not love someone who likes a good tug of war of words?<br><br>➸ <b>
  <i>Feyre’s Family:</i>
</b> A bunch of underserving and ungrateful bastards who I want to punch in the nose. Okay just kidding, they do get better so I’m allowing them to live. I might not love them, but I appreciate Elain’s kindness and hopeful optimism even in the face of her cluelessness that hurts her younger sister, and I salute Nesta’s steely will, anger, and cunning and understand her hate and coldness and pessimism, just as I want to punch her for her allowing her anger to render her useless and mourn her lost potential that will only bloom when she finds herself.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Relationships ❀</u>
</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“I love you,” he whispered, and kissed my brow. “Thorns and all.”</i>
</blockquote><br>❦ <b> <i>Romance:</i></b> I think what I value most about this retelling is how SJM confronts an ignored aspect of <i>Beauty and the Beast</i>—that it’s just as impossible and senseless as all fairytales. Look, I love B&amp;tB and it’s in fact one of my favourite fairytales, but the truth remains that <b>a character such as the Beast (<i>which I tackled in Tamlin’s character analysis</i>), with all his issues, can’t just change and heal because of a quick romance and become the perfect partner.</b> In all of Maas’s books, she’s focused healing from mental struggles upon a supporting friendship, and with <i>A Court of Thorns and Roses</i> Maas shows that without such a bond, the goal will not be reached.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I was as unburdened as a piece of dandelion fluff, and he was the wind that stirred me about the world.</i>
</blockquote><br>This romantic relationship revolves around a girl who has always protected and taken care of everyone and everything, for once letting go of control and allowing someone else to protect and take care of her. Her obedience and lack of decision-making control is at the very core of this dynamic, and it’s not right, because there will inevitably come a time in the future when what she wants isn’t what he decides she wants.<br><br><b>I applaud Sarah J. Maas for displaying this issue BUT it also results in my problem with the middle section of the book:</b> When you are shown all the reasons why you don’t want to root for a romantic relationship, then what are you supposed to do in a book heavy with it?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Two. Two was a lucky number, because that was like Tamlin and me—just two people. One had to be bad, because one was like Amarantha, or the Attor—solitary beings. One was a nasty number, and three was too much—it was three sisters crammed into a tiny cottage, hating each other until they choked on it, until it poisoned them.</i>
</blockquote><br>❦ <b> <i>Familial Bonds:</i></b> Complicated family dynamics have been the most prised additions to my bookshelves forever, and Feyre’s relationship with her sisters and father takes its place right next to the best written ones. Though, there is much left to be explored.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Worldbuilding ❀</u>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1596944503i/29938037._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Cauldron save me,<br>Mother hold me,<br>Guide me to you.<br>Let me pass through the gates;<br>Let me smell that immortal land of milk and honey.<br>Let me fear no evil;<br>Let me feel no pain.<br>Let me enter eternity.</i>
</blockquote><br>I believe there are two types of world building: <i>systematic</i> and <i>mysterious</i>. The former is the style most readers prefer, with rules and history and elements all fully explored and explained. The latter, however, <b>reads more like folklore</b>. I love both types as I see each belonging in a different type of book. And unlike her other worlds, that’s the style Maas uses for this series.<br><br>No, the mysterious style of world building isn’t the same as an underdeveloped one; <b>it’s about delivering bits and pieces of myth in rationed spoonfuls, while leaving the precise rules as unknown as muddy waters.</b> And, as fit for a fairytale, SJM applies this method in <i>A Court of Thorns and Roses</i> to start creating an alluring land of lethal creatures. If you don’t enjoy this style, you probably would not like this series. And even if you do, you still might not like it. Why?<br><br>Because <b>when it comes to faeries, there are three groups of people: <i>purists</i> and <i>progressives</i> and <i>idontreallycareeitherways</i>.</b><br><br>If you happen to be a faerie purist like my dearie faerie queen of the west <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097547101" rel="nofollow noopener">Tabs</a>, you are going to have a real problem with darling Sarah’s simultaneously more human and more animal faeries, even as their trickster, riddled nature is conserved. In that case, I’d like to kindly redirect you to <i>Holly Black</i>’s addictive <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097547101" rel="nofollow noopener">The Folk of the Air</a>
</i> series which is an all-time fave.<br><br>But, if you are a faerie progressive like my little wolf <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3473189989" rel="nofollow noopener">Xandra</a> (<i>who was wholly distressed when she thought SJM’s faeries couldn’t lie until she breathed a sigh of relief</i>) or an idontreallycareeitherway like me, then you’re just where you might belong.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1600260875i/30113965._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>❀ Companions ❀</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <i>Book series playlist:</i>
</b> <a href="https://open.spotify.com/playlist/4tJR3AqVXFpTZxp8ym0rj5" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify URL</a><br><br><b>
  <i>Books in series:</i>
</b><br>➴ A Court of Thorns and Roses (ACoTaR, #1) ★★★✯☆<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2607459551" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> (ACoTaR, #2) ★★★★★<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2609911951" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Wings and Ruin</a> (ACoTaR, #3) ★★★★☆<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2616709616" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Frost and Starlight</a> (ACoTaR, #3.1) ★★★☆☆<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2621945038" rel="nofollow noopener">Untitled Novella</a> (ACoTaR, #3.2) ☆☆☆☆☆<br>➴ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3408986917" rel="nofollow noopener">A ​Court of Silver Flames</a> (ACoTaR, #4) ☆☆☆☆☆</span>
  <a data-text-id="6088886745972765366" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2358651094" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2358651094" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2358651094?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer6853919620055683038">omg you guys. look at my original review! i totally thought tamlin was bae. im dying. oh, to be young and innocent. 2018 was such a simpler time. <br/><br/>but i still loathe nesta with every fibre of my being, so i guess some things never change. lol.<br/><br/>______________________________<br/><br/>this was serving me some major ‘beauty and the beast’ meets ‘twilight’ realness. and i had no idea that was something i needed in my life until now. i completely understand the hype around this book. all of the world building, t</span>
  <span id="freeText6853919620055683038" style="display:none">omg you guys. look at my original review! i totally thought tamlin was bae. im dying. oh, to be young and innocent. 2018 was such a simpler time. <br /><br />but i still loathe nesta with every fibre of my being, so i guess some things never change. lol.<br /><br />______________________________<br /><br />this was serving me some major ‘beauty and the beast’ meets ‘twilight’ realness. and i had no idea that was something i needed in my life until now. i completely understand the hype around this book. all of the world building, the writing, the pacing, and of course, ALL the tamlin. brilliance! it is safe to say that i am now a proud owner of a first class ticket on the SJM bandwagon. the woman is a queen. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>4.5 stars</i></b></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1022600837?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=liburry-book">liburry-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys?shelf=fairy-tales-do-they-come-true">fairy-tales-do-they-come-true</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1022600837" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12983095134934996776">Prepare to see what I felt like during the reading of this book...............................................................<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/lJlmZu2' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434929943i/15279625.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>(The original gif of the fat guy with boobs flopping in slow motion won't load. Thanks GR)<br/><br/>This shit reads slowwwwwlyyyyy. Not much happens in the entire first 2/3 of this whole book.<br/>You have Feyre who is feeding her dad and her two evil stepsisters. Oh wait, this is Beauty and the Beast not Cinderella. Anyways, her dad is pretty much spineless after losing his money a</span>
  <span id="freeText12983095134934996776" style="display:none">Prepare to see what I felt like during the reading of this book...............................................................<br><a href="http://imgur.com/lJlmZu2" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434929943i/15279625.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>(The original gif of the fat guy with boobs flopping in slow motion won't load. Thanks GR)<br><br>This shit reads slowwwwwlyyyyy. Not much happens in the entire first 2/3 of this whole book.<br>You have Feyre who is feeding her dad and her two evil stepsisters. Oh wait, this is Beauty and the Beast not Cinderella. Anyways, her dad is pretty much spineless after losing his money and the two sisters aren't going to stoop to actually feeding themselves so they all three look for the family's youngest to feed them. Feyre. The family is starving so she goes into the dark and scary woods to hunt. She sees a deer! Then a wolf! She kills them both.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/4Qrd8h0" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434929438i/15279574.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Turns out the wolf is Fae and a big bad guy shows up demanding a life for a life. He takes Feyre to live with him in his lands. <br>He turns from the monster to a fae that has a mask on due to an curse/plague/some shit. I lost interest at this point. I do know you can eat fae food. After all those books that said you can't.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/MBWDL9l" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434929438ra/15279575.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Of course, there is a curse. I don't want to go spoilery but use your imagination. It is not hard to figure out.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/ynaemCa" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434929438ra/15279576.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Then finally we get to some action. Bad evil woman has the land under her spell. Feyre has to save the day by either a riddle or completing three tasks. I like evil woman.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/OXRq6pX" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434929438i/15279577.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Evil woman saved the book from a one star just because she was a horny bitch. Yay!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12983095134934996776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RkAjpnXaZtt+ch/oW/+YMX3bg8ZXY9D1OQeFwyiaZFuSintVdQz8u9mV07FEOz3NwanjqxpBXH2M+fd0phCdgg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('57KNMNCma+acDyi3Itp0/hOCpZ9tkbQo53e5n0g2uQwzeNXD0HDxhjvo5O49HtECr/DF8iCzOKBSicsoxrxA1Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

        $('bookCover_33026517').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_33026517').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_33026517').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
